Opportunity 001 -  
Adoption of new technologies to raise operational eﬃciency
Inﬂuence scenario:
The Company adopts new technologies to enhance  operational efficiency and uses energy-
eﬃcient equipment at the terminal to improve performance and reduce carbon emissions. By 
boosting operational eﬃciency and installing energy-eﬃcient equipment, operating costs are cut, 
and the expenses for responding to climate impacts are reduced.
  
Opportunity 002 -  
Adoption of transportation methods with higher eﬃciency
Inﬂuence scenario:
The Company adopts equipment with higher eﬃciency, monitors the vessels’ sailing resistance, 
and regularly cleans hulls to allow the vessels to have good energy efficiency performance. In 
compliance with the supervisory requirements of international organizations, the Company 
improves the vessels’ sailing eﬃciency and reduces their carbon emissions, cutting operating costs.
1. Highly-efficient terminal operations: Process improvements, such 
as optimization of operating procedures, improvement of  cargo 
handling eﬃciency, and real-time workplace monitoring, and process 
change management, as well as software and hardware  upgrades 
will eﬀectively enhance the  operational eﬃciency of container yards, 
reducing energy consumption, increasing equipment availability and 
turnover, and cutting operating costs.
2. Use of low-carbon equipment: Low-carbon emission/electronic 
stackers and LED lighting equipment are used to replace outdated 
stackers using diesel fuel and electricity-consuming lighting equipment 
to reduce carbon emissions and cut potential carbon costs.
Reduced operating costs.
Replacement of machinery and equipment for reduced operating costs: 
Energy-eﬃcient lighting equipment is used and stackers using diesel fuel 
are replaced to reduce operating expenditure.
Higher capital expenditure, increased expenses.
Reduction of vessels’ fuel consumption and carbon emissions: 
Regularly cleaning hulls, monitoring main engine torque, and installing 
energy-eﬃcient propellers and bulbous bows, which allow vessels to sail 
with low resistance can reduce fuel consumption. If the EU’s Fit-55 carbon 
transaction platform and FuelEU Maritime go live and apply to ocean 
carriers in the future, carbon fees can be reduced, and penalties can be 
avoided.
Reduced operating costs.
Reduction of vessels’ fuel consumption: Regularly cleaning vessels’ 
hull and making energy-eﬃcient modiﬁcations to propellers and bulbous 
bows can reduce sailing resistance and prevent outer panels from marine 
organisms, cutting fuel consumption.
Increased expenses.

Opportunity 003 -  
Diversiﬁcation of business activities
Inﬂuence scenario:
 In response to climate change and in line with international sustainability trends, continuous eﬀorts will be put into the 
research of low-carbon transportation routes and products, investment in new energy development, etc. Diversiﬁed 
product and service development and applications as well as business diversiﬁcation can boost revenue, save costs, and 
help gain support from customers. 
2.5.3 Climate Change Metrics and Targets
 Net zero emissions by 2050 
 (long-term)
 Annual hull cleaning  
(short-term/medium-term)
1% reduction in carbon intensity in 2022 
 (short-term)
 Paying attention to the development of laws /
regulations and markets (long-term)
To support the government’s net zero emissions policy, we have 
formulated a decarbonization pathway according to our operations. 
For relevant GHG strategies towards carbon reduction, please refer to 
3.1 Environmental Management Policy.
Yang Ming picks a suitable port for underwater cleaning every year. 
The Company’s vessels are dry-docked once in 5 years to recoat their 
outer panels.
Newly-built 11,000 TEU ships were put into operation. The drydock 
time of old vessels was reduced to improve hull eﬃciency. Yang Ming 
collaborated with Weathernews Inc. in the forecasting of safe and 
fuel-saving routes, and continuously promoted the achievement of 
the carbon intensity reduction target. In 2022, the carbon intensity 
decreased by 5.15% compared to 2021. For more information about 
Yang Ming’s annual carbon intensity and emissions as well as its 
achievement of the IMO’s target, please refer to 3.3.Greenhouse Gas 
and Emissions
Yang Ming keeps an eye on the development of environmental 
regulations and market conditions every year. We have joined the 
Silk Alliance, the Getting to Zero Coalition, and the Society for Gas as 
a Marine Fuel (SGMF) to exchange opinions on technical feasibility 
and assess potential profits through risk and opportunity analysis, 
providing a foundation for future investment in new energy.
Climate Change Risk Metrics
Climate Change Opportunity Metrics
1. Launching of sailings with low-carbon energy ships: We continuously assess all possible 
alternative energy technologies and look at the feasibility of clean energy/green fuels for 
additional business sources.
2. Investment in low-carbon energy transportation equipment: Yang Ming plans to participate 
in national renewable energy programs and discusses with potential joint venture partners 
about investing in maintenance vessels for oﬀshore wind farms, LNG carriers, etc. to increase 
revenue sources.
3. Development of new routes: Low-carbon vessels are deployed to keep up with the trend of 
green corridors in the future and increase business sources. Short-distance or low-carbon 
emission routes are developed for additional business sources.

2.6 Supply Chain Management
2.6.1 Yang Ming’s Supply Chain  
          Management Vision
In view of the importance of supply chain management, 
Yang Ming has set sustainability goals based on the UN’s 
Sustainable Development Goals (SDGs), established the 
“Supply Chain Management Policy” and “Supplier’s Code 
of Conduct” according to the GRI Standards, United Nations 
Global Compact (UNGC), International Labor Organization 
(ILO) and other international standards, and encouraged 
suppliers to sign the “Company Sustainability Statement 
Survey,” inviting them to commit themselves to ethical 
management, promote environmentally sustainable 
development, and protect fundamental human rights.
2.6.2 Supply Chain Overview
Yang Ming’s supplier management covers quality, 
environmental protection, information security, occupational 
safety and health, supply chain safety, and the regulatory 
requirements of port states. While transporting the cargo 
of customers, we also pay attention to the issues of 
stakeholders’ concern, thereby fulfilling corporate social 
responsibilities together with suppliers from different 
sectors.

■ Annual Procurement Analysis
The Company analyzes the annual procurement amounts and grades/classiﬁes suppliers. In 2022, 
Yang Ming conducted procurement transactions with 1,364 suppliers, which were categorized 
into 8 types by procured items and service nature: general affairs and services, professional 
services, marine fuel, vessels, safe operation of vessels, container/chassis/genset, container yard 
machinery, and shipping-related services. The Company set a materiality threshold for each type 
by the procurement amount and transaction frequency with the suppliers and identiﬁed a total of 
166 Tier 1 suppliers, accounting for 82% of the total procurement amounts.
■ Proportion of 8 Types of Procurement Expenditure
■Proportion of 8 Types of Suppliers

operation of vessels. Also, such procurement constitutes

Vessels

procurement amounts
Vessels are the backbone of the Company’s 
international container shipping services. Their 
construction, chartering or other uses/deployment have 
direct and signiﬁcant impacts on the operation of routes.
Safe operation of vessels
Accounting for over 1% of total 
procurement amounts
Yang Ming treats personnel safety, vessel safety, and 
cargo safety as first priorities. Thus, the installation 
and maintenance of vessel equipment, the supply and 
inspection of parts and accessories, material supply and 
quality requirements, and vessel docking repairs are the 
keys to vessel sailing safety.

Accounting for over 1% of total

prerequisite for meeting the transport needs of 
customers. Also, container yard machinery are 
required to maintain the safety and efficiency of 
transport services. As such, both are important capital 
expenditures.

together constitute the global maritime transport service 
network. Yang Ming ensures the accurate connection 
of all transport links with 24/7 operation so as to oﬀer 
customers global maritime transport services that are 
punctual, speedy, reliable and economical.

● Local Procurement and Green Procurement
Marine transportation services are all over the world. As a part of the container transport industry, 
the Company oﬀers global shipping and route services as well as regional transport services (e.g., 
feeder, train, truck, and other inland transport services). Moreover, based in Taiwan, Yang Ming 
strives to ensure the procurement of general aﬀairs and services from local (Taiwanese) suppliers, 
except for procurements speciﬁc to the shipping industry, with the aim of facilitating and supporting 
the industry in Taiwan, realizing local procurement and promoting local economic growth.
Since 2013, the Company has supported the National Green Life Movement initiated by the 
Environmental Protection Administration, Executive Yuan by prioritizing the use of Green Mark-
labelled products. Yang Ming was recognized as an “Excellent Private Enterprise for Green 
Procurement” by the Keelung City Government for 2 consecutive years. The Company’s green 
procurement amount in 2022 grew 156.10% compared to 2021, accounting for 23.45% of 
the procurement amount for general affairs and services. This year, to further support the 
Environmental Protection Administration’s Green Office measures, Yang Ming has become a 
partner of the movement to put energy saving, carbon reduction, and eco-friendly philosophies 
into practice in oﬃces and incorporate them into daily oﬃce activities in an eﬀort to contribute to 
ecological protection and continuously attain the Company’s sustainable development goals.
The Company’s procurement expenditure in Taiwan in 2022 accounted for 2.40% of the total 
procurement expenditure, and green procurement accounted for 0.04% of the total procurement 
expenditure.

2.6.3 Sustainable Supply Chain Management Policy
Yang Ming adopted the “ISO 9002 International Quality Management System Certiﬁcation” in 1996 
to progressively develop operating procedures, including selection and procurement procedures 
for vessels, accessories, materials, fuels, container machines, terminals, railways/highways. We also 
receive a third-party audit annually. In 2022, to ensure sound supply chain management policies, the 
Company reviewed the existing procurement management system and identiﬁed documents whose 
amendment must be prioritized in the future based on the “ISO 20400 Sustainable Procurement” 
framework to reinforce the Company’s management of procurement governance, procurement 
principles and supplier selection. We expect to amend the following management guidelines in 2023 
for the purpose of attaining sustainability.
Management 
Aspect
Management Document
Procurement 
governance

Supplier Ethical Corporate Management Best Practice Principles
Topic
Brief Description
Human Rights 
and Workers
The Company is devoted to creating and maintaining a good working environment where 
employees are treated reasonably and with respect. Our suppliers are requested to adopt 
the same or similar standards in their working environments to ensure that the human rights 
of their employees are not affected and infringed. Relevant measures cover working hour 
management, salary and beneﬁts, employee privacy, gender and opportunity equality, child 
labor, and occupational safety and health.
Environment
Suppliers should consider environmental factors and conduct improvement and maintenance 
for impact factors in the course of operations to reduce environmental burdens and impacts. 
Relevant measures cover the management of energy consumption and GHG emissions, waste 
and wastewater management, noise management, and air pollution management.
Business 
Ethics and 
Ethical 
Management
Suppliers should observe the highest moral standards in the course of operations, expand 
relevant business activities, and develop relevant policies for internal propaganda to enhance 
their employees’ understanding of corporate ethical management policies.
■ Supplier’s Code of Conduct
In 2021, the Company formulated the Supply Chain Management Policy requesting supplier partners 
to jointly support Yang Ming’s existing ISO management systems. To build a sustainably developed 
operating environment, the Company undertakes to communicate with different supply chain 
partners about environmental protection, human rights and labor management, ethics and integrity, 
public welfare, and other issues, create comprehensive management mechanisms, and continue 
improvement and optimization eﬀorts.
On the basis of the Company’s management philosophies of “Teamwork, Innovation, Integrity, 
Pragmatism,” Yang Ming’s vision is to be an excellent transportation group in the hope of working 
with supplier partners to promote sustainable development and ensure business, financial, 
environmental and social sustainability. According to the regulations and acknowledged standards of 
the UN Global Compact, Ethical Trading Initiative, OECD, ISO 45001, ISO 27001, ISO 14001, Universal 
Declaration of Human Rights, International Labour Organization (ILO) and other international 
organizations, the Company regularly reviews and amends Yang Ming’s Supplier’s Code of Conduct 
and such amendment covers 3 parts: human rights and workers, environment, business ethics, and 
ethical management to reﬂect that the Company has acknowledged global issues and undertaken 
to comply with related standards. We also hope that our suppliers comply with these standards and 
encourage them to actively cooperate and make continuous improvements.

2.6.4 Supply Chain Management Process
01
Supplier Evaluation and Selection
When conducting transactions with suppliers, the Company requests them to comply with Yang 
Ming’s Supplier’s Code of Conduct. We also evaluate the suppliers with which we make purchases 
each year, and those with found deﬁciencies are recorded and requested to make corrections. 
Suppliers that fail to cooperate are suspended. In the annual supplier evaluation, the suppliers are 
evaluated for their contract performance to determine if the contract is renewed.
02
Supplier ESG Review
The Company plans to carry out an ESG review for Tier 1 suppliers every year by inviting them 
to complete sustainability questionnaires. The questionnaires cover 3 ESG topics, with multiple 
indicators set. The suppliers are requested to answer the questions according to the requirements 
and provide supporting information, thereby assessing their sustainable governance, social and 
environmental management maturity.
03
Sustainability Risk Evaluation
Risk quantiﬁcation and evaluation are conducted based on the sustainability review 
results of all suppliers. Their response measures and management capabilities for 
relevant issues are comprehensively issued according to the identiﬁed sustainability 
risks and threats annually to rate the suppliers as high-risk, medium-risk and low-
risk for management by risk level.
04
Supplier Engagement
On-site reviews and necessary guidance measures are performed and provided for the high-risk 
suppliers identiﬁed in the sustainability risk evaluation.
05
Tracking of Supplier Improvement
The high-risk suppliers identiﬁed in the sustainability risk evaluation result are requested to make 
improvements and propose relevant plans. The Company regularly keeps track of its improvement 
to reduce the overall supply chain risk.
● Implementation Performance in 2022
In 2022, the Company sent the sustainability self-assessment questionnaires 
to the 144 Tier 1 suppliers identiﬁed in the previous year. There were 3 topics 
and 27 indicators. We conducted written reviews for 30 suppliers answering the 
questionnaires, including 4 for general aﬀairs and services, 4 for professional 
services, 4 for marine fuel, 3 for vessels, 6 for safe operation of vessels, 1 for 
container/chassis/genset, 4 for shipping-related services, and 4 for container 
yard machinery. Among them, 2 suppliers for shipping-related services received 
on-site reviews.
● Planning of Goal Implementation in 2023
1. To increase the number of suppliers reviewed year by year, we will 
conduct written reviews for 50 suppliers in 2023, of which 5 will receive 
on-site reviews.
2. The sustainability risk evaluation will be initiated.
3. There will be an improvement tracking program for the high-risk 
suppliers identiﬁed in the sustainability risk evaluation result, thereby 
reducing the overall supply chain management risk.

Appendix
■ Supplier Evaluation and Selection
The Company assesses the qualiﬁcations of suppliers and selects them in accordance with 
the procurement and disposal procedures. For supplier selection, aside from the basic 
information of suppliers, the Company Sustainability Statement Survey and a Statement of 
Integrity in Business Operation are required, where sustainability topics such as labor rights 
practices, occupational health and safety, environmental protection, and corporate code of 
ethics are included.
Once becoming the Company’s official partners, our supplier partners must promise to 
observe all laws and regulations that should be complied with when executing their business 
activities, including but not limited to international or domestic regulations or conventions 
on labor, environmental protection, health and safety, and obtain licenses or special permits 
required to perform their business activities, including but not limited to having their 
employees meet regulatory qualification requirements and acquiring business licenses for 
businesses requiring special approval. Our supplier partners should completely understand 
the Company’s requirements for the health, safety, hygiene and employment of employees 
as well as environmental protection, confirm that they have been informed of them, and 
undertake to take corresponding safety measures. In case of any staﬀ injury/death or disaster 
during the contract period, our supplier partners should take necessary response measures 
and make a report to the Company immediately after the incident occurs. In conclusion, in the 
event of any violation of the statement or contract provisions, Yang Ming may terminate the 
contract without notice and will not collaborate with suppliers that fail to make improvements 
afterwards and are not compliant with the requirements. The Company did not cause 
negative social or environmental impacts on the supply chain in 2022.
According to the comparison among governance, social and environmental issues, environmental 
and social questions had similar scores, and governance questions got the lowest scores. The issues 
with the top 3 highest scores were related to “legal compliance,” “integrity management,” and 
“sustainable governance,” indicating that the suppliers were stronger in terms of the management 
of legal compliance, integrity management, and sustainable governance. Suppliers with lower 
scores were weaker when it came to the management of “supplier management,” “business 
continuity management,” and “energy/resource use” issues and will be provided with guidance and 
improvement advice in the evaluation in 2023.
■ Supplier ESG Sustainability Review
The Company conducted a written supplier sustainability review for the ﬁrst time in 2022, where the 
total average score of all suppliers was 49. There were 7 suppliers with a score of higher than 60, 
accounting for 23%. The percentage of suppliers with scores falling within the lowest score range 
was 3 % and those with a score of over 50 was 43%.

■ Supplier Risk Evaluation
To reinforce supply chain management, the Company plans to create a supplier risk evaluation system that is scheduled to be implemented in 2023 and provide diﬀerent management methods 
based on the risk level of suppliers in the hope of eﬀectively reducing the Company’s supplier and supply chain risks. In the ﬁrst phase, sustainability self-assessment questionnaires will be sent 
to 166 Tier 1 suppliers. The data answered by the suppliers will be converted into risk values for calculation. They are then compared with the sustainability issues identiﬁed by the Company to 
set materiality thresholds, classify the suppliers by risk level, and develop diﬀerent management methods.
■ Supplier Engagement
By enhancing the engagement with suppliers, the Company improves its sustainability capabilities while continuously boosting the Company’s supply chain resilience. In 2022, written supplier 
sustainability self-assessments using questionnaires and on-site audits were carried out for the ﬁrst time. Yang Ming distributed sustainability self-assessment questionnaires to 30 suppliers in 8 
diﬀerent categories and selected 2 suppliers for on-site audits to understand their sustainability maturity as the foundation for promoting the Company’s supply chain management system and 
building the sustainability awareness of the suppliers. Relevant measures include e.g. performing on-site inspections or providing assistance to help suppliers with poor performance in written 
reviews develop necessary systems. In the future, we will increase the number of suppliers reviewed year by year so as to drive the compliance of the overall supply chain with ESG indicators.

2022 compared to 2008
Reduced the fuel consumption by 356,492 tons or 21.5% 
through eﬀective shipping schedule control
90.32% of Yang Ming’s vessels achieved an estimated CII 
rating of C or higher
Used water-based paints for all newly-built containers, 
reducing up to 2,657 tons of VOCs
Promoted digitalization to cut paper use, reducing about 
3.93 tons of CO2e
Reduced the water consumption of offices and container 
terminals by 9.23% compared to 2021 and cut the volume 
of waste by 17.77% compared to 2021, with a 11.01% 
increase in the recycling rate
Entered into systematic collaboration with National Cheng 
Kung University to obtain 1 invention patent
Received the highest Sapphire award in 2022 in recognition 
of Yang Ming’s support for the Protecting Blue Whales & 
Blue Skies Program

3.1 Environmental Management Policy
Yang Ming upholds the core value of achieving environmental sustainability through energy saving 
and emissions reduction. We were the ﬁrst ISM-certiﬁed carrier in Taiwan in 1996 and implemented 
the ISO 14001 environmental management systems in 2004. Through a series of environmental 
protection measures, the Company has been dedicated to protecting marine ecology, reducing 
carbon emissions, and air pollution in an eﬀort to ensure a better environment for future generations. 
By carrying out ﬂeet renewal, deploying new eco-friendly vessels, optimizing ship sailing attitudes, 
adjusting cargo ballasting and ensuring energy-eﬃcient draft operation based on stowage planning 
practices, working with WNI using big data cloud technologies, and other intelligent technologies to 
enhance operational eﬃciency through monitoring by the Smart Ship Center, reinforcing ﬂeet carbon 
reduction management, monitoring the energy consumption performance of vessels, refining 
the existing vessels for better energy eﬃciency, the carbon intensity of the Company’s operating 
vessels in 2022 was 40.21 g/teu-km, reduced by up to 59.54% compared to 2008, exceeding the 
target of the IMO. The fleet not also uses shore power to reduce air pollution, but also conducts 
wastewater discharge control and lowers ship speed to maintain local marine ecology. Furthermore, 
the Company supports the Environmental Protection Administration’s Green Oﬃce measures, and 
the oﬃces and the Keelung (Yang Ming) Container Yard adopt energy saving and carbon reduction 
measures to enhance the eﬃciency of energy utilization and implement local procurement, green 
procurement, and source reduction in order to lower energy use and reduce resource waste.
To implement specific commitments and strategies to achieve net zero emissions by 2050, the 
Company conducted a GHG inventory in 2021 as the base year for the Company’s total carbon 
emissions and deployed LNG dual-fuel container ships. In 2022, Yang Ming became a founder 
member of the Silk Alliance and joined the Getting to Zero Coalition and the Society for Gas 
as a Marine Fuel to work with the companies in the shipping industry chain in developing fuel 
transformation and sustainable decarbonization strategies in the hope of serving as a sustainability 
leader in the global shipping industry.
● Use of Shore Power to Reduce the Impact of Vessels on the Environment
Yang Ming’s American investee company West Basin Container Terminal (WBCT) has developed 
and managed 16 alternative maritime power (AMP) systems that not only comply with federal and 
local laws and regulations, but also meet the specifications of the California Air Resources Board 
(CARB), improving the air quality in harbor areas. The Company’s vessels equipped with shore power 
equipment actively cooperate with ports such as the Port of Los Angeles, Port of Long Beach, and Port 
of Oakland in initiating shore power connections. With these AMP systems, container ships can use 
on-shore power when calling at the ports, reducing the air pollution produced by generators.
Moreover, the Company’s Kao Ming Container Terminal Corp. is an eco-friendly container terminal 
using green energy and equipped with 6 AMP systems for use by container ships when calling at the 
port. In addition, Kao Ming actively cooperates with the Environmental Protection Administration 
in shore power promotion to facilitate the development of environmental protection businesses in 
Taiwan.

3.2 Energy Use and Consumption
Due to the Company's implementation of appropriate energy management measures, 
despite a 12% increase in business volume in 2022, there was no signiﬁcant increase in the 
total heating value. The energy intensity was 0.137 (GJ/NT$ thousand), reduced by 9.00% in 
comparison to 2021.

■ Energy Conservation Strategies

Fleet

     prepare records as per laws in order to save energy and reduce carbon emissions. 
● Smart Ship Center - Monitoring with the Green Shipping Module. 
● Determination of optimal routes with weather routing systems. 
● Foundation of the CII Task Force in 2022 to pay attention to the actions and  
     regulations of international organizations such as the IMO.
Energy Conservation Measures at Yang Ming’s Oﬃce in Cidu
The Company has adopted various energy conservation facilities and actions since 2010. The 
number of employees grew in response to the expanded corporate business scope. Even though 
the number of employees in the oﬃce building in Cidu where Yang Ming’s headquarters are located 
was increased by 36% in 2022 compared to 2010, the annual electricity consumption dropped 11%. 
The following are some energy conservation measures adopted:
●Setting up programs for group control of the 4 elevators, where the elevators will enter sleep 
      mode when not in use for 10 minutes for energy conservation.
●Setting up the water dispensers on each ﬂoor to automatically keep them in sleep mode from 
      23:00 to 06:00 on weekdays and all day on weekends.
●Using water chiller units of diﬀerent tons for the central air conditioner in the building based on 
    seasonal and temperature requirements and setting up the auto power-on time of the air-handling 
    unit on each ﬂoor and the frequency converter for automatic input regulation according to needs.
●Setting up printers in power saving mode to have them automatically enter power saving mode 
     when not in use for a period of time.
●Setting up oﬃce computers in power saving mode to have them automatically enter low-power- 
     consuming sleep mode after not in use for 5-10 minutes.
● Fleet’s Energy Use
The IMO approved the new “Energy Efficiency Existing Ship Index (EEXI)” and “Carbon Intensity 
Indicator (CII)” regulations at the MEPC 76 meeting held via video conference from June 10 to 
17, 2021, which will take effect on January 1, 2023. For the IMO’s strategies to reduce the GHG 
emissions of vessels, on the technical aspect, the EEXI is adopted; on the operational aspect, the CII 
is adopted. By calculating the “EEXI” and “CII,” correction plans are developed for vessels with poor 
performance, and the vessels are included in the SEEMP.
In addition to making cross-departmental discussions on EEXI regulations to develop an appropriate 
inspection schedule and reduce the carbon emissions of vessels based on the maximum engine 
power limit after construction, the Company’s CII Task Force (across 9 departments including the 
Marine Department, Operations Department and Engineering Department) founded in September 
2022 checks the CII ratings of vessels on each route to timely monitor the change of the CII ratings 
and annual fuel consumption with digital tools and holds regular meetings every month to discuss 
the timing of adopting the 21 rating optimization measures for the vessels to tackle problems at the 
source. Each ship aims at obtaining a CII rating of C in the current year.

accounting for 90.32%:

The following are the measures adopted by the Company in response to the EEXI and CII:
■ New Vessels’ EEDI
The EEDI of the Company’s newly-built vessels are higher than that speciﬁed by the applicable regulations. In 2022, ﬁve new vessels were delivered, and all of them are EEDI certiﬁed. The 
management practices mentioned above are compliant with regulatory requirements and undergo an external audit annually.

3.3 Greenhouse Gas and Emissions
3.3.1 Greenhouse Gas 
According to the IMO’s statistics, the global shipping industry produces over 1 million tons of CO2 
emissions every year, accounting for about 2.9% of the CO2 emissions worldwide. The shipping 
industry plays an important role in reducing global carbon emissions. In recent years, the UN 
Climate Change Conference and EU have called for the control of global warming at 1.5 ℃, and 
many international initiatives and organizations have encouraged enterprises to set reduction 
targets and measures in response to the goal of net zero emissions by 2050. Yang Ming has actively 
promoted green shipping. In 2021, the Company introduced the ISO 14064-1 GHG inventory and 
acquired third-party verification. Based on the inventory results, we promoted and planned the 
setting of GHG emission reduction targets and measures for the Company. In 2022, the Company 
continued to complete the ISO14064-1 GHG inventory for the vessels owned and operated by the 
Company, which was third-party veriﬁed and Taiwan Accreditation Foundation (TAF)-certiﬁed.
■ GHG Inventory Results
The increase in the total Category 1 emissions was due to a 12% increase in business volume, 
but the overall carbon intensity was reduced by 4.91%. To reduce fuel consumption by vessels, 
the Company increased the use of shore power at ports of call, leading to an increase in the total 
Category 2 emissions and a 2.33% rise in the overall carbon intensity. In order to better control the 
Company’s Category 3 emission data year by year, the Company’s GHG inventory was expanded 
this year, which was the main cause for the change in the total Category 3 emissions.

● Management of Vessels’ Carbon Emissions
Yang Ming continues to go above and beyond international regulatory requirements by adopting 
management measures such as hull optimization, the introduction of new eco-friendly vessels, 
optimal ship speed control, the use of smart monitoring systems, and the modiﬁcation of existing 
ships. The CO2 emission intensity of the operating vessels in 2022 was reduced by 59.54% compared 
to 2008, early attaining the IMO’s goal of a 40% reduction by 2030 and proceeding towards the goal 
of a 70% reduction by 2050.
Although the ﬂeet’s CO2e in 2022 was 102,194.7764 (tCO2e) higher than that in 2021, the carbon 
intensity was reduced by 2.14 g/TEU-km, showing a 5.05% improvement, thanks to the fact that the 
unit transport volume in 2022 was higher than that in 2021.

3.3.2 Air Pollution Emissions
The sulfur limit of the International Maritime Organization (IMO) requires that the content of sulfur in ship fuels shall not exceed 0.50%. Since it took eﬀect in January 2020, all ocean carriers 
have been under enormous pressure in terms of reducing SOx emissions. Yang Ming’s ﬂeet met the requirement early in the fourth quarter of 2019. Compared to the heavy fuel oil formerly 
used, the newly-used fuel’s SOx emissions have been reduced by 86%. As of 2022, 44% of the Company’s vessels have been installed with desulfurizers, and 56% have used low-sulfur fuels. The 
average unit emissions of NOx and SOx were reduced by 5.17% and 8.3%, respectively, in comparison to 2021.
■ Air Pollution Emissions 
In 2022, in continuation of Yang Ming’s support of environmental protection and air quality improvement, all newly-manufactured containers used water-based paints, eﬀectively reducing 
VOC emissions by 2,657 tons. In addition, in both on-shore or onboard operating activities, the equipment and consumables used by the Company do not emit ozone depleting substances. For 
example, all the Company’s own reefer containers newly-manufactured in 2022 started to use the R134a refrigerant, reducing about 428 kilograms of emissions as compared to when the R404a 
refrigerant was used for container repair in 2021. This demonstrated the Company’s attention and eﬀorts given to air pollution control.

3.4  R&D and Investment in Low-Carbon  
        Technologies
With the deepening awareness of environmental protection worldwide, such as the IMO’s 
annual carbon intensity reduction targets or the European Union’s goal of achieving a 75% 
GHG reduction by 2050 compared to the relative base year 2020, Yang Ming has been actively 
dedicated to low-carbon technology investment and R&D, paid continuous attention to the 
development of low-carbon industries, sought opportunities to invest in clean energy and 
relevant transport ships in a pragmatic manner, and adopted a variety of strategies including 
developing the deployment of alternative fuels, researching energy-eﬃcient technologies for 
vessels, and engaging in industry-academia collaboration, welcoming the challenges of global 
zero carbon emissions and attaining the goal of green sustainability.
  Development of Alternative Fuels
We have kept an eye on the technical maturity of diﬀerent alternative fuels for ships 
(e.g., biofuel, methanol, hydrogen, ammonia), the vertical integrity of the supply 
chain, and the development of international environmental protection regulations. 
The Company initiated the deployment of ﬁve 15,000 TEU LNG power-driven dual-
fuel container ships. The carbon emissions of LNG are about 20% less than those 
of conventional fuels. Moreover, to develop alternative fuels with higher maturity, 
we chose to build LNG-powered dual-fuel vessels which are cleaner as our new 
ships in the hope of not only reducing carbon emissions, but also enhancing the 
overall operating competitiveness of the ﬂeet. Since 2023, Yang Ming has arranged 
basic and advanced LNG and engine model training for excellent seed seafarers to 
obtain certiﬁcates for the IGF CODE.
For the research of energy-eﬃcient technologies for vessels, the Company has put 
in continuous efforts and gained progressive outcomes. Currently, the research 
focuses on carbon capture devices, bubble drag reduction, energy-efficient 
wind shields, energy-efficient propellers, shaft generators, and exhaust/waste 
heat recycling systems. While assessing the maturity of relevant infrastructure 
(e.g., refueling ports), fuel supply chains, and main engine/electric machinery 
technology development, Yang Ming will continue investing resources in seeking 
the innovation and breakthrough of energy-eﬃcient technologies to help achieve 
the goal of green shipping.
Industry-Academia Researches
In 2022, Yang Ming obtained an invention patent for the “Method for 
Predicting Fuel Consumption of Ship” (I792418) together with the Systems 
and Naval Mechatronic Engineering of National Cheng Kung University. This 
research was initiated jointly by Yang Ming, National Cheng Kung University, 
and CSBC Corporation, Taiwan in 2016 to execute the Ministry of Science 
and Technology’s “Data Analytics for Smart Shipping and Marine Energy 
Management” project. Lasting 3 years, the project developed an energy 
efficiency program to verify the energy efficiency and maintenance cycle/
eﬀect of each ship and mark the operating range of onboard main engines, 
electric machinery, or vessel shafts, thereby enabling continuous monitoring. 
In case of any abnormality, alarms can be sent to onboard operators and 
onshore managers. It is hoped that through data mining, we can identify 
important factors that may affect the energy efficiency performance of 
vessels objectively, create hull health assessment models, and predict power 
consumption in order to formulate eﬀective energy eﬃciency improvement 
strategies.
In response to the goal of net zero emissions by 2050, the Company has 
been actively looking for low-carbon alternative fuels. Yang Ming and National 
Taiwan Ocean University’s “YM-NTOU Framework – Yang Ming Think Tank” 
has been commissioned to assess the feasibility of using methanol as an 
alternative fuel for container vessels in the future. The use of methanol will 
be taken into account for the future deployment of next generation energy-
eﬃcient vessels.

Low-carbon Investments for Onshore Business Locations
Installation of green  
electricity production units  
in the business building
Chongqing Building has commissioned professional contractors to design 
an eco-friendly and energy-efficient green roof where there will be an 
aquaponics system, green plants, and a recreational trail and to introduce 
green energy and rainwater recycling systems, which can produce an eﬀective 
heat insulation eﬀect and thereby reduce the AC energy consumption of the 
building.
The expected outcomes are: 
● 3,960 kWh of annual solar power generation. 
● 134 metric tons of rainwater recovered per year. 
● 2,016 kilograms of carbon emissions reduced per year.
Vehicle electriﬁcation
Electric motorcycles are used as company vehicles, and the existing company 
cars have been replaced with hybrid electric vehicles in a stepwise manner. 
A hybrid electric vehicle consumes 3 L/100km less than a conventional one. 
It is expected that 600 liters of fuel can be saved for all our company cars 
throughout the year. 
Electriﬁcation of  
container yard equipment
We completed the installation of new-model gantry cranes and the 
rearranging of the loaded container storage area in the Keelung (Yang Ming) 
Container Yard in 2022.
● The energy eﬃciency and safety of the new-model gantry cranes have been 
veriﬁed by the American Bureau of Shipping and TÜV Rheinland
®. Power 
can be supplied to the gantry cranes through power cables, reducing 
power loss during power transmission where, in the past, relay substations 
were required and lowering the average energy consumption of each load 
and unload of a container. The power consumption of modern gantry 
cranes is only one-sixth of that of old-model ones. We also stopped using 
diesel rubber-tyred gantry cranes, reducing about 95 thousand liters of 
diesel annually, equivalent to a reduction of 248.40 tons CO2e.
● Rearranging and renovation of the loaded container storage area: Yang 
Ming was the ﬁrst to place the container pickup lane in the middle of the 
storage area to shorten the distance that gantry crane trolleys have to 
move, enhancing pickup eﬃciency. Loaded containers are placed on both 
sides of the lane, and cement and steel-reinforced container pads are used 
to deal with the rainy weather in Keelung and avoid stacking the containers 
on the waterlogged ground, effectively reducing the risk of moisture 
damage to cargo. The area has a storage capacity of 2,160 TEUs, and 
there are 336 reefer container plugs for import/export and transshipment 
containers, which eﬀectively expands the service capacity of Yang Ming at 
Keelung Port.
3.5 Waste Disposal and Ship Demolition  
       and Recycling
As Yang Ming has developed more energy-eﬃcient vessels and continued the expansion of service routes 
as a leading global ocean carrier, the replacement of old ships with new ones and the increasing waste 
production volume as a result of rising demand have become important issues. Eﬀective management 
is achieved through policy development and by sorting, disposing of and recording/controlling the waste 
produced in the course of operations as well as disposing of decommissioned vessels.
Onshore Waste  
Management Measures
1
Waste sorting and recycling are performed to ensure proper waste disposal and thereby 
improve the quality of recycled items.
2
Employees are encouraged to bring their own cutlery and avoid using one-time use cutlery.
3
Environmental propaganda and education are promoted to foster employees’ environmental 
protection awareness.
4
Employees are encouraged to bring their own cups and get an appropriate amount of food 
for lunch to avoid waste and reduce kitchen waste.
5
Promotion of paperless work: If possible, all business documents are handled and stored 
electronically. The Company has promoted paperless attachments to vouchers payable and 
digital shipowner bill management, improved the agents’ cloud utilization rate, and used 
electronic import receipts, contributing to a reduction of about 3.93 tons CO2e. Printing on 
both sides of paper is also requested to make the most of waste paper.
6
We commission qualified disposal vendors to dispose of general waste. Each operating 
premise should dispose of its waste in accordance with the environmental protection 
regulations of the respective county or city.

Vessel Waste  
Management Measures
1
The sorting/collection and handling of onboard waste comply with the related regulations in 
Annex V to the International Convention for the Prevention of Pollution from Ships. Waste 
management plans have been formulated for the ﬂeet to handle hazardous waste and solid 
waste produced onboard. The plans cover 5 main procedures: collection, sorting, handling, 
storage, and recording.
2
All food residues are properly handled according to conventions and the laws of port states.
3
In addition to reducing waste and hazardous substances, waste batteries/chemicals/waste 
bulbs/medical waste are disembarked for recycling and disposal.
4
There are stainless steel garbage bins onboard for waste sorting. The waste storage area is 
disinfected and cleaned regularly.
Yang Ming has a green ship recycling policy in place. When it comes to disposing of 
decommissioned vessels, the Company complies with the Hong Kong Convention (HKC) 2009. 
We also protect the health and human rights of workers as well as the marine environment in 
accordance with the requirements in the following table. The Company did not carry out any 
ship demolition activities in 2022.

their progress in 2022 are as follows:

3.6 Wastewater/Sewage Discharge  
       Management
Water resources are another issue that Yang Ming gives particular focus. The Company 
strictly complies with the water resource regulations stipulated by the competent authorities 
in business locations and the international regulations of the IMO and MARPO in terms of the 
use of water resources and discharge.
■ Water Resource Management Measures
3.7 Biodiversity
During transport, to maintain vessel stability, “ballast water” is pumped in, if necessary, to keep the 
vessel balanced. However, as the ballast water may carry local aquatic organisms, a “ballast treatment 
system” is required to remove the aquatic organisms and pathogens contained in the ballast 
water and sediments in order to avoid aﬀecting the marine environment and ecological balance. In 
accordance with the International Convention for the Control and Management of Ships' Ballast Water 
and Sediments (BWM), Yang Ming has installed ballast water treatment equipment on the vessels and 
created a new edition Ballast Water Management Plan (BWMP) for review and delivery to the vessels. 
Relevant ballast water management practices are subject to Port State Control (PSC) inspections to 
meet the requirements of all port states.
The research project titled “Research and Discussion on the Ballast Water Treatment Methods 
Applicable to Cargo Ships” was commissioned by Yang Ming and National Taiwan Ocean University 
to the “YM-NTOU Framework – Yang Ming Think Tank” in 2022 to analyze the cost-eﬀectiveness and 
biological treatment eﬀect of chemical agents in treating vessel ballast water. Through such research 
plans, the ballast water treatment mechanism for the Company’s vessels is reviewed in a strict and 
responsible manner. We also continue to look for more appropriate ways to reduce the impact of 
ballast water on marine ecology.In 2022, there were no events with serious leaks or release 
of vessel waste into nature.

■ Plan for Vessel Speed Reduction to Protect Blue Whales
Between May and November every year, to prevent vessels from colliding with blue whales, 
humpback whales, fin whales, and other endangered large marine animals in Southern 
California and San Francisco Bay waters and allow the whales to migrate to the waters for 
foraging, the Company decreases the speed of the ﬂeet to below 10 knots in continuation of 
the Company’s support of the “Protecting Blue Whales & Blue Skies” Program hosted by the 
National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration (NOAA) since 2016. In recognition of Yang 
Ming’s eﬀort, we were presented with a Sapphire award which is the highest honor in 2022.
■ Great Barrier Reef Protection
The Company’s vessels call at the Port of Sydney, Port of Melbourne, and Port of Brisbane in 
Australia. In sailing all the way from any Asian port to the aforementioned ports, low-sulphur 
fuels containing less than 0.5% of sulphur are used. Instead of the core waters of the Great 
Barrier Reef, our vessels navigate the Particularly Sensitive Sea Area waters east of the Great 
Barrier Reef according to route recommendations from Weathernews Inc. to conserve the 
coral reef, demonstrating Yang Ming’s contribution and determination to protect the marine 
ecological environment.
■ Asian Gypsy Moth Regulations
The Company’s ﬂeet observes the announcement on Asian gypsy moths (AGMs) made jointly 
by the United States Department of Agriculture (USDA), Animal and Plant Health Inspection 
Service (APHIS), and Canadian Food Inspection Agency (CFIA) to take the following measures 
for vessels docked in the AGM supervision area during the certain risk period:
●Accredited certiﬁcation bodies inspect the vessels and certify that they are free of AGMs.
●The vessels should arrive at the ports in Northern America free of AGMs. To avoid facing 
route changes, being asked to leave port for cleaning, and being potentially affected in 
terms of reducing the risk of AGMs entering Northern American, carriers should conduct 
frequent vessel inspections themselves to identify and remove (scrape oﬀ) any AGM egg 
masses and AGMs in any state of development. All found AGM egg masses and AGMs 
should be properly treated or destroyed before entering any American and Canadian ports.
●The vessels should provide a list of ports that they called at in the past 2 years to their 
Canadian or American agents at least 96 hours before arrival at any Northern American 
ports.
The bamboo flooring of the Company’s containers must meet Yang Ming’s testing 
requirements. Before assembly, the ﬂooring undergoes permanent preservative treatments 
according to the container quarantine and inspection procedures of the Australian Federal 
Departments of Health and Transport and in accordance with the Australian Quarantine and 
Inspection Service’s requirements. After use, all containers must be fully cleaned and free 
of organic substances in compliance with the requirements of the Institute of International 
Container Lessors (IICL) in each pre-trip inspection. In addition, new, tin-free ship paints are 
used for hulls to avoid ocean pollution, maintaining biodiversity.

4.1 Navigation and  
      Transportation Safety  
4.1.1 Cargo Transport Safety
To ensure that cargo can be delivered to any point worldwide safely, Yang Ming 
strictly observes all international conventions such as the SOLAS, MARPOL, CSC 
and IMDG Code and complies with countries’ laws and regulations on cargo and 
dangerous goods in cargo arrangement and transport. Aside from abiding by 
the conventions and laws and regulations, the Company has introduced WNI’s 
professional weather routing system for transportation to gain access to the safest 
route recommendations. All employees operating the system are required to 
receive various education and training courses to build complete knowledge of 
navigation and transportation safety and abilities to operate professional systems 
and software. With the aforesaid multiple control measures, the Company’s cargo 
transport safety is eﬀectively ensured.
According to statistics, there were 2 incidents 
reported through the “Cargo Incident 
Notification System (CINS)” in 2022. In both 
incidents, the export customers involved 
intentional undeclaration of cargo in the 
e-booking stage and the bill of lading, resulting in the containers emitting 
smoke during shipping. The Company’s subsequent handling measures 
are described below:
1.The subsequent shipping of the containers emitting smoke was 
immediately terminated after they were discharged at the port.
2.We included the customers in the blacklist and identiﬁed other bookings 
that they made right away to discharge all of them at the port and 
terminate the shipping contracts with them early.
3.The commodity  of the undeclared cargo  in these bookings were added 
to the database as high-risk keywords for reviewing new bills of lading 
in the future. Meanwhile, the other recent bills of lading were reviewed 
once again through the system to check if there were same commodity 
names.
4.Penalties were imposed on the customers according to the Company’s 
notice of penalties for undeclaration by customers.
5.The commodity of the undeclared cargo were circulated to all our 
representatives in Asia to raise their awareness of freight safety.
6.The loading arrangement was revised to regulate that any cargo with 
the same commodity as the cargo involved in the undeclaration shall 
only be shipped on deck.
■ Yang Ming’s Safe Transportation Process
■ Education and Training
A l l  s t a f f  m u s t  r e c e i v e

■ Sailing Safety Monitoring
● When any stowage safety issues are found after departure, either of the following   
     3 actions is taken to solve concerns about subsequent sailing:
▶ Fix the issues through cargo restow at the next port.
▶ Return to the loading port.
▶ Look for the nearest port to solve the safety issues.
● When the captain ﬁnds that there are risk concerns about synchronous rolling or parametric rolling during 
     navigation, necessary actions will be taken immediately, such as changing the sailing direction or speed.
■ Pre-departure Safety Checks
● Cargo safety
Seafarers and onshore employees use Class certified stowage software and the software 
equipped with the Apply Speciﬁc Route & Short Voyage and Lashing Force Checking functions 
in order to view all types of cargo safety data and conduct Lashing Force and Max Stack Weight checking.
● Route safety
Weather routing systems are used for access to safe route recommendations provided by professional 
companies, reducing concerns about vessel sailing safety caused due to weather factors.
● Pre-loading cargo inspections and veriﬁcation:
▶ After stowage planners receive pre-stowage plans, they use the Pre-Plan Checklist (PPC) to check the pre-
stowage plan on an item-by-item basis to ensure compliance with all safety requirements.
▶ If any incompliant stowage plan is found, the planners at the terminal should modify it and send the modiﬁed 
pre-stowage plan to the onboard/onshore personnel for veriﬁcation of all safety data.
▶ Only after the seafarers conﬁrm that there is no safety issue may cargo be loaded.
▶ When the port of loading ﬁnds that the actual stowage is inconsistent with the pre-stowage plan, which leads 
to safety concerns, after the cargo is loaded, it should ask for correction immediately.
■ Review and Improvement
● Regular review and experience sharing:
▶ A monthly stowage safety management meeting is held regularly to review the causes of  
    abnormal incidents, eliminate the causes of cargo restow, and share stowage experiences. 
● Yang Ming has joined international organizations consisting of shipowners to discuss transport safety issues.

4.1.2 Special Cargo Transportation
To enhance cargo transport safety and attain the goals of personnel safety, vessel safety, 
and cargo safety, Yang Ming has set up a professional dangerous goods management team 
responsible for strictly carrying out safety inspections for loading dangerous goods containers on 
ships (including for alliance partners). All containers with dangerous cargo must undergo loading 
data review and approval procedures to conﬁrm that all related international conventions and 
port regulations & limitations on dangerous goods are complied with before loading.
The YM DG Policy has been developed with the following rules taken into account: 
In addition to the main 3 rules, the Company has also incorporated the professional knowledge 
and suggestions on the dangerous properties of cargo provided by the Cargo Incident Notiﬁcation 
System (CINS) into the YM DG Policy to make revisions from time to time.
For all dangerous goods containers carried by the Company, relevant data should be in place 
and submitted to the Operations Department for review. The containers will not be approved 
for loading unless the declared data is compliant with the requirements of the IMDG CODE 
and YM DG Policy. If our alliance partners intend to apply for loading dangerous goods on Yang 
Ming’s vessels, the goods may be loaded on the ships only after the same review procedures are 
completed.
■ Key Points for Dangerous Goods Management
1.Prohibited goods under the IMDG CODE
2.High-risk cargo
3.Cargo having a high frequency of abnormal incidents during shipping and is prohibited from  
    shipping by most carriers
Thanks to the strict control of the navigation and transportation safety of each batch of 
dangerous goods, the Company did not violate the IMDG Code and the dangerous cargo 
loading/discharging operation regulations of each port in transporting dangerous goods in 
2022. For labeling violations by customers, there were 6 dangerous goods containers violating 
the labeling speciﬁcations of the IMDG CODE in 2022. As the liabilities were attributed to the 
shippers, the Company asked the customers to bear relevant derivative costs.
■ Detection and Defense System (DDS)
This undeclared cargo detection system is developed by Yang Ming together with an 
external developer. The Company also maintains a keyword database containing the 
commodity and fictitious of undeclared dangerous goods to detect suspicious bills of 
lading. Shipping instructions (SI for short) and oﬃcial bills of lading are reviewed before 
loading on the vessel. In addition to containing the names of dangerous goods in the IMDG 
Code, this database is updated by the members of the dangerous goods management 
team from time to time to add the of undeclared goods. Bills of lading are scanned using 
this system on a daily basis. If there are any keywords for suspicious goods or undeclared 
dangerous goods in any bill of lading, the actual commodity of such batch of cargo 
suspected to be dangerous goods will be tracked immediately, and the customer is further 
required to provide the related documents of the product for veriﬁcation to rule out the 
doubt that the cargo is undeclared dangerous goods. If it is veriﬁed that the commodity 
provided by the customer in the declaration is consistent with the name of the actual 
products in the container, this batch of cargo will be allowed to be loaded on the vessel 
according to the original shipping schedule; if it is verified that the cargo is undeclared 
dangerous goods, the agent at the port of loading is notiﬁed immediately to cancel the 
loading arrangement to prevent the loading of undeclared dangerous cargo on the 
vessel, thereby enhancing the transport safety of dangerous goods. There were 24 cargo 
concealment incidents identified in 2022.

■ Education and Training
Vessels’ stowage planning and stowage safety have been key issues highly discussed 
recently. Maritime organizations and countries around the world strictly ask container 
carriers to treat the issues as ones of the important shipping affairs and safe operational 
practices. To enhance the professional knowledge of maritime workers on the transport 
of dangerous goods containers, the Company has designed online education and training 
courses on dangerous goods based on the IMDG CODE and organized the “Training on 
Operational Safety for Dangerous Goods” and “Case Studies of Abnormal Incidents related to 
Related to Dangerous Cargo Transportation” courses to meet the mandatory basic dangerous 
good training requirements of the IMDG Code for relevant workers, thereby improving 
the safety of cargo control. Relevant professional courses and training are used to boost 
maritime workers’ knowledge of business activities related to dangerous goods and their risk 
awareness for dangerous goods.

■ Smart Ship Dynamics Management
4.2 Digital Transformation
4.2.1 Smart Ship Center( War Room)
Yang Ming’s newly designed smart ships are incorporated with big data servers collecting 
voyage data and actual engine room operating data to monitor the speed and sailing 
schedule of ships and predict their sailing conditions in the future. Weathernews Inc. and 
supervision captains are in charge of monitoring the dynamics of the ships, and weekly 
meetings are held regularly for reporting. The energy eﬃciency performance of every ship in 
the ﬂeet is monitored in a real-time manner through the data reported by Power BI. On the 
shore side, the energy eﬃciency performance is managed through satellite networks. Data 
analysis is conducted and equipment health and potential risks are also assessed to reduce 
fuel consumption while saving energy and reducing carbon emissions.
In response to the Company’s digital transformation strategy, Yang Ming’s vessels have 
introduced systematic information systems to eﬀectively organize the existing information/
data and administrative procedures of the ﬂeet in order for the shore side to monitor ﬂeet 
management synchronously. Phase 1 of the War Room Smart Ship Center project was 
completed. The information on the ﬂeet is now available for search through LINE Chatbot. 
The information systems of all units have been integrated in a stepwise manner to organize 
the information on the systems for subsequent tracking and improvement.
■ 3 Phases of the Smart Ship Center (War Room) Project from 2021~2029
Weather integration
Weather software is integrated into the Smart 
Ship Center to help the ﬂeet to identify hazardous 
weather conditions as early as possible in order 
to adjust routes and reduce risks
Real-time dynamics
Relevant important information is displayed 
in real-time and linked to ship position 
dynamics to help maritime personnel make 
correct and timely decisions
Vessel supervision app and platform
The supervision cycle is integrated to record the 
process from arranging supervision, data returning, 
boarding for the supervision, to completing the 
supervision on the system and allow for the tracking 
of improvement plans and conditions at any time
Cross-platform integration
Information is integrated in a cross-platform 
manner by introducing several systems, 
including a seafarer supervision management 
system, to facilitate the control of vessel sailing 
information and enhance vessel management
Fleet management platform
After our own fleet management 
platform was built, we included all 
types of information in the platform 
to eﬀectively control our vessels and 
increase operational resilience
Data alerting system
All safety indexes of vessels 
are monitored in real-time 
to improve vessel safety

4.2.2 Digital Transformation
To better service our customers, Yang Ming established a global business intelligence platform 
as part of the digital transformation program. This platform is a decision-making support 
system that integrates a variety of big data on customers, vessels, containers, terminals, 
etc., and collects real-time information from system mainframes and various databases to 
optimize system eﬃciency, visualize the information to enable employees to get insights from 
reporting tools easily and conveniently. The platform also helps the management team make 
better business decisions by feeding more timely and accurate market intelligence.
■ Digital Transformation of  Accounts Payable Management and Auditing Procedure
Yang Ming has actively implemented digital transformation, made the accounting procedure with 
shipowners go digital and paperless, and used this as the KPI for evaluating the performance 
of Yang Ming’s agents worldwide. The Company’s agents and suppliers around the world are 
required to provide e-bills in PDF or EDI without printing paper vouchers to reduce the use of 
international delivery services to send the bills to regional centers and the headquarters in Taiwan 
for auditing. The Cloud FS (Cloud File Server) has also been created to store e-bills. The Company 
has collaborated with external R&D vendors and professional consultants in introducing digital tools 
OCR (optical character recognition) + RPA (robotic process automation). In particular, the OCR rate 
can come up to 98%. The process from receiving bills from shipowners and suppliers to completing 
the auditing process is integrated.
■ Yang Ming’s achievements for digital and paperless billing with shipowners 
     worldwide in 2022 are shown in the following table

● Yang Ming’s E-Customer Service System
In recent years, the contactless economy and remote working have become the new normal, 
and digital transformation has been mainstreamed in the post-pandemic era. The Company has 
continuously innovated parts of the overall logistics system, striving to provide customers with 
more convenient and smoother service experiences. As of this year, we released several widely 
acclaimed services, including LINE Chatbot, an intelligent documentation system, e-D/O (electronic 
delivery order), digital telex release bills of lading, and e-Counter. In 2022, in addition to optimizing 
the services mentioned above, we launched a brand-new mobile version of the E-Service app. The 
app was newly equipped with a mobile e-booking function to allow customers to make an e-booking 
at any time, anywhere, can be opened via Siri for real-time cargo tracking and tracing, and was 
designed to be used on Apple watches. The functions of the mobile E-Service app the customers 
use the most are shown in the following table:
The Company was engaged in cross-industry cooperation with multiple banks in Taiwan, 
being the country’s leading carrier in the execution of proofs of concept on blockchain and 
international trade, and successfully accelerated the shipping and trading/ﬁnancing processes 
through blockchain technology. Moreover, document digitalization allows customers who 
need to work from home or staggered shifts to deal with import/export business activities 
remotely during the pandemic, saving printing and delivery costs.

■ Yang Ming’s e-Service Types
Improved from the conventional inquiry method via phone in the past, the 
instant messaging inquiry service allows customers to check the latest vessel 
and container movement information via LINE Chatbot on the phone.
• In 2022, there were about 500 inquiries made through 
the LINE Chatbot services of the Keelung (Yang Ming) 
Container Yard, Taiwan Business Department and Hong 
Ming Terminal & Stevedoring Corp. on average per day, 
equivalent to reducing the number of works by about 3.
Delivery orders (i.e. “D/O”) are stored on the cloud for import customers to 
download, streamlining the complicated import D/O exchange process and 
reducing time of the import pick-up process by at least half a day.
• In 2022, e-D/O accounted for about 30.25% of import 
delivery orders. 50,089 paper import delivery orders 
were reduced, cutting about 0.32 tons of CO2e and 
reducing approximately 93 working days spent for 
printing and binding.
To address the need for travel due to the diﬀerence between the D/O receipt 
and pick-up sites, Yang Ming oﬀers an e-Voucher service that enables customers 
to speed up and simplify the transmission of delivery orders through cellphone 
authentication, eﬀectively improving the speed and timeliness of the customers’ 
import process.
• In 2022, electronic vouchers used accounted for up to 
15.38% of e-D/O.
The Company worked with multiple banks in Taiwan in launching the e-Counter 
service to cope with the communication limits resulting from the pandemic. 
The digital transformation of conventional import/export processes has been 
conducted e.g. by moving payment and D/O receipt processes online to increase 
customers’ operational speed and timeliness and avoid the risk of contact 
between the customers and partners.
• In 2022, the online reservation services had a utilization 
rate of 89.74%, and it was estimated that 213 tons of 
carbon emissions and 2.1 tons of paper ink could be 
reduced and saved from exchanging bills of lading with 
customers.
Digital telex release bills of lading have saved nearly 70% of costs in paper and 
toner from export bills of lading for Taiwanese enterprises, allowing customers 
to speed up the process without working over the counter.
• Overall, up to 70.43% of export bills of lading were 
digitalized in 2022, reducing 41,261 paper bills of lading 
and cutting about 0.26 tons of CO2e.
Online customer manifest write-oﬀ services are provided to allow shippers and 
customs brokers to complete the manifest write-off process online, not only 
saving the time and labor costs required for over-the-counter services, but also 
reducing the pick-up time by about half a day.
• 80.25% of time spent by the ﬁeld team of Yang Ming’s 
Keelung Branch on manifest write-oﬀ has been saved, 
equivalent to cutting about 1-1.5 employees/day.
The service was released in 2022, enabling customers to make price inquiries 
online 24/7 without being subject to nine-to-ﬁve working hours. Digital forms 
are created to reduce manual work and simplify work ﬂows.
• Total number of members worldwide signing up for My 
Ocean Freight during 2022/5/6-12/31: 637.
A version with a brand-new look and refined functions was launched in 
2022, providing users with a fresh user experience. Functions that allow for 
more convenient and faster e-booking submission and acquisition of cargo 
information were added.
• The new version of the app has been installed 4,583 
times. For its detailed use, please refer to Yang Ming’s 
E-Customer Service System.

■ Import/Export Customer E-Services in Taiwan
In recent years, to deliver more convenient and optimized services for customers, the Company has rolled out innovate digital services combined with e-Counter and RPA (robotic process automation)-based 
automatic reconciliation in place of manual OTC reconciliation, saving about 2 minutes per transaction, as well as e-D/O (an invention patent for the “Information System for Processing Delivery Order and 
Method and Serving Method Thereof” (I741895) was obtained in 2021) and online manifest write-oﬀ services for Keelung (Yang Ming) Container Yard (an invention patent for the “Container Terminal Pick-up 
Method, Container Terminal Computer, and Pick-up Information System” (I792933) was obtained in 2022), oﬀering the customers online one-stop import pick-up services that allow shippers to exchange the 
bill of lading, write oﬀ the manifest, and dispatch freight drivers for pick-up without having to be on site personally or exchange the bill of lading for a delivery order. The online services not only increase the 
convenience of import processes, but also reduce the pick-up time of the shippers by more than half a day.

■ Employee Training and Upskilling for Digital Technologies
In response to advancing digital technology tools and services, the Company has been constantly seeking opportunities in optimizing and innovating customer service  in digital form.  To ensure success, 
transformation of company culture through talent development, employee upskilling and education of digital technologies is being done on an ongoing basis. In 2022, 62 events were organized, including 
digital technology lectures, collaborative platform tutorials, and experience sharing workshops, with 10,344 participants. In addition to training courses, the Company has organized Power BI contests  and 
activities to foster employees’ digital technology competencies and familiarizing them with the global business intelligence platform, enhancing eﬃciency in day to day operations, and building a long-term 
competitive edge.

4.3 Information Security and Customer Privacy
A sound information security mechanism not only can enhance operational resilience, but 
also serves as the backbone for customer privacy protection. In 2022, Yang Ming did not have 
any substantiated complaints about breaches of customer privacy or losses of customer data. 
Furthermore, to ensure the protection and security of operational information, the Company has 
been certiﬁed to ISO 27001:2013 Information Security Management System. Management review 
meetings are held annually to implement information security activities and review the progress 
of goal achievement and risk mitigation in the current year to make sure that the Company’s 
information is safe and secured. The management review meetings are chaired by the Chairman 
or the person designated thereby and attended by relevant departmental oﬃcers. An ISO 27001 
external audit is conducted every year to ensure that the Company’s management systems and 
their performance comply with the requirements of the ISO. In response to changing information 
security issues and protection system improvements, the Company expects to update the 
certiﬁcate to the ISO 27001:2022 version in 2024.
In compliance with Article 9-1 of the “Regulations Governing Establishment of Internal Control 
Systems by Public Companies,” the Company appointed a Chief Information Security Oﬃcer to set 
up the “Cyber Security Oﬃce” in 2022, which is responsible for information monitoring, supervision, 
management and tracking as well as information security strategy development. In 2022, Yang Ming 
initiated a series of information security programs internally, such as password strength increase, 
MFA, Zero Trust, and additional data encryption. We also plan to extend the programs externally to 
other operation-related units afterwards. In an eﬀort to boost information security management 
strength, the Company has adopted fortress-like information security strategies and progressively 
expanded them in the following four directions:
■ Maintenance and Control of Yang Ming’s Information Security
■ Fortress-like Information Security Strategies
■ Information Security Management Review Meeting Procedure
Management review results should be recorded and retained according to related 
regulations.

One management review meeting is held annually and chaired by the Chairman or the 
person designated thereby. The participants include relevant departmental officers. At the 
meeting, relevant information and results are reported, and the implementation suitability, 
appropriateness and eﬀectiveness of the information security management system is reviewed.
A management review meeting agenda includes:
■ How past management review proposals have been   
      handled.
■ Change of internal and external issues related to the  
      information security management system.
■ Feedback on information security performance.
■ Feedback from interested parties.
■ Status of risk evaluation results and risk  
      treatment plans.
■ Opportunities for continuous improvement.
Management reviews should come up with decisions related to opportunities for 
continuous improvement and see if there is any necessity to make changes to the 
information security management system.

of coding security risk is expanded to prevent potential

■ Information Security Risk Evaluation
According to the requirements in the Company’s information security policy, an information 
security risk evaluation is conducted regularly every year to assess and determine the level of risk 
based on internal/external information security issues, the probability of occurrence, the level of 
impact, and the level of inﬂuence scale. The evaluation covers system infrastructure, system change 
management, project and resource management, asset and physical environment management, 
software/hardware license and compliance. After the evaluation is completed, treatment measures 
are developed against high-risk items and presented at a management review meeting.
● Information Security Outcomes
■ Information Security Education
To enhance employees’ knowledge of information security, the Company 
organizes at least 3 social engineering exercises and 1 online information 
security promotion education and training session for all employees annually 
to raise personnel’s information security awareness and protect the 
Company’s information assets from disruption, damage, intrusion or any 
other malicious behavior. For diﬀerent personnel categories, diﬀerent information security 
education and training methods are planned and shown in the following table:
■ Information Security Reporting and Handling
To timely respond to and handle information security incidents, employees may report any 
incidents they encounter at any time. After receiving a report, the Information Security Team 
categorizes and handles the incident based on its type.
■ Information Security Response Exercise Plan
Units start to count the number of machines infected, engage in communication and 
coordination, and adopt a response plan immediately from the point where the Security 
Operation Center reports/the system detects/a user reports a computer or network anomaly. 
With the aim of enhancing the Company’s information security attack tolerance, exercises 
are performed to review the process, increase personnel’s familiarity with the practices of 
each stage, and revise the response and restoration plan.

■ Vessel Information Security
Yang Ming’s smart vessel information security management focuses on the following 3 points:
The Company issued a vessel information security manual in 2021. As of the end of 2022, 49 vessels in the ﬂeet introduced corporate information security monitoring center services. The vessel 
information security system is audited by a third-party body regularly. Social engineering exercises and training are organized for seafarers, and those who fail in the exercises and training are 
required to participate in remedial education and training. In 2022, no property loss occurred to the ﬂeet due to information security.
To maintain customer privacy and navigation and transportation safety, the Company developed the Vessel Information Security War Room system to monitor the use of all data in real-time. 
The system is also used as an important line of defense against information security anomalies to ensure the provision of safe and secured customer services and experience.
1. Incorporate ISM management and designate vessel information security officers.
2. Obtain information security certificates for the engine room monitoring systems provided by smart vessel equipment suppliers.
3. Work closely with communication companies in information security monitoring
